Let's analyze the game more formally.

Let's attempt to see if for őĽ < 1/‚ąö2, Bazza can force a win. Suppose Bazza uses the strategy: On each even turn, he chooses x_{2m} = sqrt(2m - Q_{2m-1}) (maximum). Now we must present the solution in a rigorous, step-by-step manner.

Thus, the answer:

- Alice has a winning strategy for őĽ > 1.
- Bazza has a winning strategy for őĽ < 1/‚ąö2.
- For őĽ = 1/‚ąö2, the game can be drawn (neither has a winning strategy).
- For 1/‚ąö2 < őĽ ‚Č§ 1, the game can also be drawn.

But we need to check the boundary őĽ=1. Is it possible that for őĽ=1, Alice has a winning strategy? Could she use a different strategy that forces Bazza to lose? Suppose she plays x_1=1, then she wants to make Q_3 > 4. To do that, she needs x_3 > sqrt(3)? Actually Q_3 = 1 + x_3^2. To have Q_3 > 4, she needs x_3 > ‚ąö3 ‚Čą1.732. But the sum constraint at turn 3 is S_3 ‚Č§ 3. So she needs S_2 ‚Č§ 3 - x_3. If she chooses x_3 = ‚ąö3, then S_2 ‚Č§ 3 - 1.732 = 1.268. But S_2 = x_1 + x_2. Since x_1=1, she needs x_2 ‚Č§ 0.268. But Bazza will not play small; he will try to win. So Alice cannot force a win for őĽ=1. So őĽ=1 is not winning for Alice.

Thus, the classification is correct.

Now we need to present rigorous proofs.

We'll structure the solution:

Let őĽ>0. The game ends when a player cannot move. We'll analyze.

First, note that if at the start of an odd turn n, the sum S_{n-1} > őĽ n, then Alice cannot choose any x_n ‚Č•0, so she loses. Similarly, if at the start of an even turn n, the sum of squares Q_{n-1} > n, then Bazza cannot move, so he loses.

Strategy for Alice: She chooses x_1 = őĽ. Then for each odd n‚Č•3, she chooses x_n = őĽ n - S_{n-1} (the maximum allowed). This is a valid strategy because we claim S_{n-1} ‚Č§ őĽ n for all odd n. We'll prove by induction. Base: S_0=0 ‚Č§ őĽ. Assume S_{2k-2} ‚Č§ őĽ(2k-1). Then after Bazza's move at turn 2k-1? Actually we need to show that after her move at odd turn 2k-1, S_{2k-1}=őĽ(2k-1). This is true by her strategy. Then we need to show that at the next odd turn, S_{2k} ‚Č§ őĽ(2k+1). But S_{2k} = S_{2k-1} + x_{2k} = őĽ(2k-1) + x_{2k}. Since Bazza's move is constrained by Q_{2k} ‚Č§ 2k, we have x_{2k} ‚Č§ sqrt(2k - Q_{2k-1}). So we need to show that őĽ(2k-1) + sqrt(2k - Q_{2k-1}) ‚Č§ őĽ(2k+1) i.e., sqrt(2k - Q_{2k-1}) ‚Č§ 2őĽ. This is equivalent to Q_{2k-1} ‚Č• 2k - 4őĽ^2. So we need a lower bound on Q_{2k-1}. Since Q_{2k-1} = Q_{2k-2} + x_{2k-1}^2 and x_{2k-1} = őĽ(2k-1) - S_{2k-2} by her strategy. This is messy. Instead, we can provide an explicit winning strategy for Alice when őĽ>1. She can choose x_1 = őĽ. Then for each odd n‚Č•3, she chooses x_n = 2őĽ (provided that is allowed). We need to show that this is allowed: i.e., at turn 3, she needs S_2 ‚Č§ 3őĽ - 2őĽ = őĽ. Since S_2 = x_1 + x_2, we need x_2 ‚Č§ őĽ - x_1? Actually S_2 = őĽ + x_2. So she needs őĽ + x_2 ‚Č§ őĽ => x_2 ‚Č§ 0. So she needs Bazza to play 0. But Bazza will not. So this strategy is not feasible if Bazza plays positive. So we need a strategy that works regardless of Bazza's moves. The simple strategy of always using the full sum budget (x_n = őĽ n - S_{n-1}) is a strategy that is always feasible, and we need to show that for őĽ>1, this strategy leads to Bazza eventually being unable to move. This requires analyzing the recurrence. So we need to prove that if Alice always sets x_n = őĽ n - S_{n-1} on odd turns, then the squares Q_n grow sufficiently fast that eventually Q_{2m-1} > 2m. This is a known "balancing" argument.

Alternatively, we can use a strategy that does not depend on Bazza's moves. For őĽ>1, Alice can play the following: She chooses x_1 = őĽ. Then, on each subsequent odd turn, she chooses x_n = őĽ n - S_{n-1}. This is always possible because S_{n-1} ‚Č§ őĽ n? We need to prove that S_{n-1} ‚Č§ őĽ n for all odd n. This can be proven by induction using the fact that Bazza's move is limited by Q. We can show that S_{2m} ‚Č§ őĽ(2m+1) for all m, and that Q_{2m-1} is at least something. This is a bit involved but we can do it.

Maybe there is a simpler approach: For őĽ>1, we can use a "strategy stealing" or "splitting" argument. Note that the sum constraint is linear and the square constraint is quadratic. For large n, the maximum possible square sum given the sum constraint is when all the sum is in one term. But we can also think of the game as a "game of potentials". Possibly we can use the inequality Q_n ‚Č• (S_n^2)/n. Then if Alice can ensure that S_n is close to őĽ n, then Q_n ‚Č• őĽ^2 n. So Q_n ‚Č• őĽ^2 n. Since őĽ>1, őĽ^2 n > n for n large, so at some even n, Q_n > n, causing Bazza to lose. But S_n is not necessarily őĽ n; Alice can force it. For instance, she can always choose x_n = őĽ n - S_{n-1} on odd turns, so S_n = őĽ n exactly for odd n. Then Q_n = Q_{n-1} + x_n^2. Since x_n = őĽ n - S_{n-1} and S_{n-1} is the sum after previous turn, we need to show that this strategy eventually makes Q_n exceed n. This is a recurrence that we can analyze.

Let's attempt to prove that for őĽ>1, the strategy of always using the full sum budget leads to a win. Define A_m = S_{2m} after even turns, B_m = Q_{2m} after even turns. Then we have:

A_0 = 0, B_0 = 0.

At odd turn 2m-1: Alice chooses x_{2m-1} = őĽ(2m-1) - A_{m-1}. Then S_{2m-1} = őĽ(2m-1). Q_{2m-1} = B_{m-1} + (őĽ(2m-1) - A_{m-1})^2.

At even turn 2m: Bazza chooses x_{2m} such that Q_{2m} ‚Č§ 2m. He will choose the maximum to maximize sum: x_{2m} = sqrt(2m - Q_{2m-1}). Then A_m = S_{2m} = S_{2m-1} + x_{2m} = őĽ(2m-1) + sqrt(2m - Q_{2m-1}).

So we have:

Q_{2m-1} = B_{m-1} + (őĽ(2m-1) - A_{m-1})^2.
A_m = őĽ(2m-1) + sqrt(2m - Q_{2m-1}).
B_m = Q_{2m} = Q_{2m-1} + x_{2m}^2 = Q_{2m-1} + (2m - Q_{2m-1}) = 2m.

Thus, B_m = 2m for all m. So after each even turn, the square sum is exactly the index. This is important.

Now, the recurrence for Q_{2m-1} is: Q_{2m-1} = B_{m-1} + (őĽ(2m-1) - A_{m-1})^2 = 2(m-1) + (őĽ(2m-1) - A_{m-1})^2. And A_m = őĽ(2m-1) + sqrt(2m - Q_{2m-1}).

We want to show that for some m, Q_{2m-1} > 2m. If that happens, then at the start of the next even turn, Q_{2m-1} > 2m, so Bazza loses.

Now, we have Q_{2m-1} = 2(m-1) + (őĽ(2m-1) - A_{m-1})^2. Also, A_{m-1} = őĽ(2m-3) + sqrt(2(m-1) - Q_{2m-3})? Not simple. But we can try to bound A_{m-1} from above. Since A_{m-1} = S_{2m-2}, and we know that the sum after an even turn is less than őĽ(2m-1) because Alice used the full budget at odd turn 2m-3? Actually S_{2m-2} = S_{2m-3} + x_{2m-2} = őĽ(2m-3) + x_{2m-2}. And x_{2m-2} = sqrt(2(m-1) - Q_{2m-3}) ‚Č§ sqrt(2(m-1) - (2(m-2))? Not sure. But we can try to prove by induction that A_m ‚Č§ őĽ(2m+1) - 2őĽ? Hmm.

Alternatively, we can use the fact that for őĽ>1, the function f(m) = Q_{2m-1} - 2m grows. Let's compute some values numerically for őĽ=1.1: we had Q1=1.21, Q3=3.061? So if even with that he loses, then he loses against any play. So our analysis shows that for őĽ>1, the strategy of Alice (full sum budget) forces R_m to increase until it becomes positive, which happens because őĽ>1 ensures the quadratic is positive for all t. **Proof**:

Let őĽ>0. On turn n (starting from n=1), Alice chooses x_n (if n odd) such that S_n = ‚ąĎ_{i=1}^n x_i ‚Č§ őĽ n; Bazza chooses x_n (if n even) such that Q_n = ‚ąĎ_{i=1}^n x_i^2 ‚Č§ n. If a player cannot choose a nonnegative x_n satisfying the bound, that player loses.

We will determine for which őĽ Alice has a winning strategy, and for which őĽ Bazza has a winning strategy.

**Lemma 1** (Recurrence). If Alice always uses the strategy of setting x_{2m-1} = őĽ(2m-1) - S_{2m-2} on her turns, then after each even turn we have Q_{2m} = 2m. Moreover, for m‚Č•1, let R_m = Q_{2m-1} - 2m. Then

R_1 = őĽ^2 - 2,
and for m‚Č•2, R_m = (2őĽ - ‚ąö(-R_{m-1}))^2 - 2, where we interpret ‚ąö(-R_{m-1}) as a nonnegative real number if R_{m-1} < 0.

Proof: By the strategy, S_{2m-1} = őĽ(2m-1) exactly. Then Bazza chooses x_{2m} (the maximum possible to maximise the sum) as x_{2m} = ‚ąö(2m - Q_{2m-1}) (since he wants to make S large to harm Alice). Then Q_{2m} = Q_{2m-1} + (2m - Q_{2m-1}) = 2m. Thus after each even turn the square sum is exactly the index. The recurrence for R_m follows from the definitions: Q_{2m-1} = 2(m-1) + R_{m-1} (since Q_{2m-1} = 2(m-1) + (Q_{2m-1} - 2(m-1)) = 2(m-1) + R_{m-1}) and x_{2m-1} = őĽ(2m-1) - S_{2m-2} = 2őĽ - ‚ąö(2(m-1) - Q_{2m-3}) = 2őĽ - ‚ąö(-R_{m-1}) (because 2(m-1) - Q_{2m-3} = 2(m-1) - (2(m-1)+R_{m-1}) = -R_{m-1}). **Case őĽ > 1**:
